## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics (nonlinear oscillators)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration, with state variables position x and velocity v evolving in time t, which is the standard phase-space description of (possibly damped/driven) nonlinear harmonic oscillators. Typical relationships decompose dv_dt into restoring forces (functions of x), damping (functions of v and sometimes x), and external/parametric forcing (functions of t).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear undamped oscillator (SHO): dv_dt = -c0 * x (restoring force proportional to displacement)
- Linear viscous damping: dv_dt = -c0 * v - c1 * x (damped harmonic oscillator)
- Time-dependent linear damping: dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) * v - c3 * x (damping modulated in time)
- External sinusoidal forcing: dv_dt = -c0 * v - c1 * x + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (driven damped oscillator)
- Constant bias / gravity-like offset: dv_dt = -c0 * v - c1 * x + c2 (equilibrium shifted by constant acceleration)
- Duffing (cubic stiffness, hardening/softening): dv_dt = -c0 * v - c1 * x - c2 * x**3 (nonlinear spring restoring force)
- Quintic stiffness extension: dv_dt = -c0 * v - c1 * x - c2 * x**3 - c3 * x**5 (stronger nonlinearity at large amplitude)
- Nonlinear (quadratic) drag: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v * Abs(v) (aerodynamic-like damping, always dissipative)
- Cubic velocity damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * v**3 (nonlinear dissipation increasing with speed)
- Van der Pol oscillator (state-dependent damping): dv_dt = c0 * (1 - c1 * x**2) * v - c2 * x (self-excited oscillation / limit cycle)
- Rayleigh oscillator (velocity-dependent negative damping at small v): dv_dt = -c0 * x + (c1 - c2 * v**2) * v (another canonical limit-cycle model)
- Parametric excitation (Mathieu-type): dv_dt = -c0 * v - (c1 + c2 * cos(c3 * t)) * x (time-periodic stiffness leading to parametric resonance)
- Dry (Coulomb) friction model: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * sign(v) (stick-slip style dissipation; sign may be approximated by tanh(c3 * v))
- Nonlinear stiffness saturation: dv_dt = -c0 * v - c1 * x / (c2 + x**2) (restoring force weakens/softens at large |x|)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative restoring force → dv_dt depends mainly on x and is an odd function of x for symmetric potentials (e.g., terms like x, x**3, x**5).
- Viscous dissipation → damping terms are typically odd in v (e.g., -c*v), ensuring energy loss regardless of direction of motion.
- Aerodynamic/turbulent drag → use v*Abs(v) rather than v**2 to preserve sign and always oppose motion.
- Hardening vs softening spring behavior → +x**3 in restoring force (i.e., dv_dt includes -x - x**3) tends to harden; -x + x**3 can soften depending on sign conventions/coefficients.
- Self-excited limit cycles → state-dependent damping that is negative near the origin and positive at large amplitude, commonly (1 - c*x**2)*v or (c - c*v**2)*v.
- External periodic driving → additive sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) terms in dv_dt; resonance appears when driving frequency matches natural frequency.
- Parametric resonance → time-periodic coefficients multiplying x (or v), e.g., (c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*x, producing instability tongues (Mathieu behavior).
- Dry friction / stick-slip → near-constant magnitude opposing motion, modeled by sign(v) or smooth approximations like tanh(c*v), often causing non-smooth dynamics.

GT: F0*sin(t) - beta*log(Abs(v) + c0) - omega0**c1*x*exp(-Abs(x))
Candidate formulas: 50

GT is the fixed function
\[
-1.1449635767559\,x e^{-|x|}\;-\;0.445567501246416\,\log(|v|+1)\;+\;0.10853689295113\,\sin(t).
\]
So any matching candidate must be able to reproduce simultaneously:

1) a **pure** \(\sin(t)\) term (no extra \(t\)-dependence elsewhere unless it can be zeroed),
2) a **log of \(|v|+1\)** (absolute value is essential; also the “+1” is inside the log),
3) an \(x\)-term of the specific form \(x e^{-|x|}\) (again absolute value is essential and it is inside the exponent),
4) and **no other surviving dependence** on \(x,t,v\).

Now check candidates:

GT Equivalence Verification (PO23)
============================================================
GT: F0*sin(t) - beta*log(Abs(v) + c0) - omega0**c1*x*exp(-Abs(x))
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []

I need to compare each candidate against the ground truth:

**GT:** `-1.1449635767559*x*exp(-Abs(x)) - 0.445567501246416*log(Abs(v) + 1) + 0.10853689295113*sin(t)`

Key components of GT:
1. `x*exp(-|x|)` term
2. `log(|v| + 1)` term (since v ≤ 0, `|v| = -v`)
3. `sin(t)` term

No dependence on `t` outside of `sin(t)`, no polynomial terms in `t`, `x`, or `v` alone.

Let me analyze each candidate systematically. The GT has three specific basis functions: `x*exp(-|x|)`, `log(-v + 1)`, and `sin(t)`. Any candidate must be able to reproduce exactly these three basis functions (and no others that can't be zeroed out).

**Critical observation:** The GT contains `x*exp(-|x|)`. This is NOT the same as `x*exp(c*t)` for any constant `c` (unless we can set the coefficient to 0, but then we lose the `x*exp(-|x|)` term). None of the candidates contain `exp(-|x|)` or `exp(-Abs(x))`.

Let me check if any candidate contains `log(v)` or `log(-v+1)` type terms:

- **Candidate 9:** Has `c5*log(c6*v + 1)`. Since v ≤ 0, with c6 < 0, this gives `log(-c6*(-v) + 1) = log(|c6|*|v| + 1)`, which matches `log(|v| + 1)` if |c6| = 1. But it also has `x*exp(c1*t)` which cannot match `x*exp(-|x|)` — these are fundamentally different functions (one depends on t, the other on |x|).

- **Candidate 21:** Same issue — has `log(c6*v + 1)` but `x*exp(c1*t)` instead of `x*exp(-|x|)`.

The fundamental problem across ALL candidates is that NONE of them contain `x*exp(-|x|)` or anything equivalent. They all have either:
- `x*exp(c*t)` — depends on t, not |x|
- `x/(c+x)` — rational, not exponential decay
- `exp(c*t)/(c+x)` — wrong structure
- Other structures that cannot produce `x*exp(-|x|)`

Since `x*exp(-|x|)` is a function of x alone with exponential decay based on |x|, and none of the candidates have any term involving `exp(f(x))` where f depends on x, none can match.

Let me verify there's no candidate with `exp` of something involving `x`:
- Candidate 42 has `exp(c5*x)` but no `x*exp(...)` and it's missing the log term structure.
- No candidate has `x*exp(c*x)` let alone `x*exp(-|x|)`.

Even `x*exp(c*x)` cannot equal `x*exp(-|x|)` for all x (positive and negative), since x takes both signs and |x| is not linear in x.

Therefore, NO candidate can match the GT.
